+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human
+created: 2026-07-13
+updated: 2026-07-13
+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human
+created: 2026-07-13
+updated: 2026-07-13
+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human
+created: 2026-07-13
+updated: 2026-07-13
+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human
+created: 2026-07-13
+updated: 2026-07-13
+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human

+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human

+updated: 2026-07-13
+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human
+created: 2026-07-13
+updated: 2026-07-13
+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

+---
+id: 006-cli-json-contract
+title: CLI JSON behavioral contract
+status: awaiting-human
+created: 2026-07-13
+updated: 2026-07-13
+parent: 005-improvement-survey
+children: []
+related: [003-cli-json]
+---
+
+# CLI JSON behavioral contract
+
+## Problem
+
+Proposal P2 identified that the existing CLI JSON spec does not define how a caller requests JSON, what successful or
failed output contains, or which exit status accompanies each outcome. Those are externally observable compatibility
choices and cannot be implemented safely from the current one-line requirement.
+
+## Goals
+
+- Define an invocation contract that an automated caller can test.
+- Define versioned success and error output that a caller can parse without inspecting human-readable text.
+- Define exit statuses and sensitive-data behavior for every documented outcome.
+
+## Non-goals
+
+- Implementing the CLI or changing production code.
+- Selecting the business operations or domain fields exposed by the CLI.
+- Defining interactive formatting, colors, or progress output outside JSON mode.
+- Adding streaming or multi-record output unless a later requirement explicitly selects it.
+
+## Requirements
+
+- R1. `(assumes Q1)` WHEN a caller selects the chosen JSON invocation, the CLI SHALL emit machine-readable JSON for
that invocation and SHALL emit no human-oriented decoration on the JSON output stream.
+- R2. `(assumes Q2)` WHEN an operation succeeds in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit exactly one JSON value matching the
chosen versioning and success-envelope schema.
+- R3. `(assumes Q3)` WHEN an operation fails in JSON mode, the CLI SHALL emit a parseable error value on the chosen
stream with the chosen stable error fields and SHALL keep human diagnostics off that stream.
+- R4. `(assumes Q4)` WHEN an operation completes, usage validation fails, or execution fails, the process SHALL
return the selected exit status for that outcome.
+- R5. `(assumes Q5)` WHEN JSON output is produced, the CLI SHALL apply the selected sensitive-data policy to
credentials, tokens, and secret-bearing fields.
+
+## Open questions
+
+- [ ] Q1. How does a caller request JSON output?   A: `--json` on existing commands (recommended: preserves normal
human output and is conventional); B: a dedicated `json` subcommand (clear separation but duplicates command routing);
C: JSON is always the default (smallest surface but breaks human-oriented output). Class: consequential external CLI
contract.
+- [ ] Q2. What is the success shape?   A: a versioned envelope such as `{ "version": 1, "ok": true, "data": ... }`
(recommended: supports compatible evolution and consistent parsing); B: the operation's raw JSON value (compact but
inconsistent across commands); C: newline-delimited records (stream-friendly but inappropriate for single-result
operations). Class: consequential external data contract.
+- [ ] Q3. How are JSON-mode errors represented?   A: one versioned error envelope on stdout while diagnostics go to
stderr (recommended: one parseable result channel); B: the JSON error on stderr (keeps stdout success-only but forces
callers to parse two streams); C: no JSON error body, exit status only (simple but loses structured failure details).
The structured options would include stable `code` and `message` fields; operation-specific details remain optional.
Class: consequential external and failure contract.
+- [ ] Q4. Which exit-status taxonomy should callers rely on?   A: `0` success, `2` invocation/validation error, `1`
all execution failures (recommended: distinguishes caller mistakes without a broad taxonomy); B: `0` success and `1`
any failure (simplest but less actionable); C: a documented multi-code taxonomy by failure class (most expressive and
highest compatibility burden). Class: consequential external process contract.
+- [ ] Q5. What sensitive-data policy applies to JSON output?   A: omit credential/token/secret fields by default with
no override in this increment (recommended: safest stable contract); B: mirror the source object unchanged
(transparent but may expose secrets); C: redact known secret fields with a literal marker (preserves field presence
but can be mistaken for data). Class: consequential security/privacy behavior.
+
+## Decisions
+
+- 2026-07-13: Improvement survey proposal P2 selected by the user and routed from `005-improvement-survey` to `plan`
because the missing choices are consequential external contracts.
+- 2026-07-13: No defaults were adopted for Q1-Q5; each remains parked for human selection under the
consequential-contract/security rubric.
+
+## Acceptance criteria
+
+- [ ] AC1 (R1): `(assumes Q1)` Given a supported command, when it is invoked through the selected JSON mechanism,
then its designated machine-output stream contains JSON without human decoration.
+- [ ] AC2 (R2): `(assumes Q2)` Given a successful operation in JSON mode, when output is parsed, then exactly one
value conforms to the selected version and success schema.
+- [ ] AC3 (R3): `(assumes Q3)` Given a failed operation in JSON mode, when the selected result stream is parsed, then
the error value contains the selected stable fields and no human diagnostic text is mixed into that stream.
+- [ ] AC4 (R4): `(assumes Q4)` Given one success, one invocation/validation failure, and one execution failure, when
each process ends, then its status matches the selected taxonomy.
+- [ ] AC5 (R5): `(assumes Q5)` Given source data containing representative credential, token, and secret-bearing
fields, when JSON output is produced, then those fields follow the selected sensitive-data policy.

tokens used
